  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_99e0a0cf-a260-4b3a-9ff7-3ab29216a1e9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<div id="review_730189215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730189215" />
    <a title="Myth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7449118-myth"><img alt="Myth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562794786p2/7449118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/730189215?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Myth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Myth" href="/user/show/7449118-myth">Myth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7449118-myth?shelf=assassin-rolls-do-it-better">assassin-rolls-do-it-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7449118-myth?shelf=1-5-stars">1-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer730189215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6975832632320152882">Confession time: for most of this novella, I couldn't remember why I hated this one so much more than all the others. There are sincere emotional moments, Celaena is by and large more bearable, mostly because this remains the only story where an anti-slavery viewpoint is actually woven into the character. The romance is ridiculous, but honestly at this point I handwave ridiculous romance in YA as long as it's not AWFUL romance. Plus, we get actual backstory on Celaena (which is actually sort of </span>
  <span id="freeText6975832632320152882" style="display:none">Confession time: for most of this novella, I couldn't remember why I hated this one so much more than all the others. There are sincere emotional moments, Celaena is by and large more bearable, mostly because this remains the only story where an anti-slavery viewpoint is actually woven into the character. The romance is ridiculous, but honestly at this point I handwave ridiculous romance in YA as long as it's not AWFUL romance. Plus, we get actual backstory on Celaena (which is actually sort of a problem: we should have this information in the series, not have to read companion novels for it, but that's a different issue entirely). True, Celaena hated all other women for being women still, so it was getting docked points for that, but except in one specific case it was milder than other novellas.<br /><br />Then, dear readers, I hit the last chapter.<br /><br />Remember that one specific case? That case is Lysandra. Those who have read the later books know that Lysandra and Celaena eventually become bosom buds, partly because the novels can't seem to stop commenting on Lysandra's bosom but also because the novels decide that Lysandra feels bad for unspecified behavior and apologizes, and in turn Celaena apologizes for throwing a knife at her head.<br /><br />I mean I, personally, would find knife hurling an overreaction in response to behavior not involving, say, murder or torture or rape, but these books like to think knife throwing and fire hurling are appropriate responses for mild jabs and appropriate commentary, so whatever. In this novella, we learn about the knife throwing incident. <br /><br />The knife throwing incident is in response to Lysandra telling Celaena something she already knew, ie that Arobynn used the money Celaena gave him to buy off her indenture from him to pay for Lysandra's 'Bidding' (aka, purchasing the first time Lysandra has sex)(the books' definition of sex is a narrow one, before you ask).<br /><br />The novella treats this as a 'take that'. Please keep in mind that Lysandra has been raised by Arobynn in a way similar to Celaena without the status of getting to call herself his niece (which indicates to me at least that he was specifically grooming Lysandra, which is supported in the novels themselves). She was also purchased as a small child to <i>be</i> raised that way. Could Celaena not have realized this? I would consider it possible, if we did not in fact know that Celaena is in possession of this information. SO THAT'S GREAT.<br /><br />Furthermore, the entire sordid affair is treated by Celaena, Arobynn, Sam, Lysandra, AND THE BOOK, as a personal wrong done to Celaena, because Arobynn used the money she paid off her indenture with. Is she upset that he used her money to continue a terrible practice akin if not outright identical to slavery? No. She is upset that he used the money to win Lysandra's Bidding <i>specifically</i>. The quote? "He'd spent <i>her</i> money on a person he <i>knew</i> she hated."<br /><br />Take a chill pill, Celaena and Novella. Consider for two seconds how traumatizing it must have been for Lysandra to have her virginity bought and 'taken' by her father figure and then maybe consider that you're both tied for The Actual Worst.<br /><br /><br /><br />Also, you had 166 fragments in 104 pages. Hope you're happy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6975832632320152882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Her plans for a grand speech with sweeping gestures faded into silence. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>Of all the people in the world, only Arobynn knew the absolute truth. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>She couldn’t tell what was worse: a quick beheading, or yielding to the king. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>The Mute Master had told her that people dealt with their pain in different ways—that some chose to drown it, some chose to love it, and some chose to let it tu</span>
  <span id="freeText13649493745689305605" style="display:none"><b>A sneak peek into the dysfunctional dynamics between Arobynn and Caelena.</b><br /><br />Q:<br />Seconds passed, then minutes. Her plans for a grand speech with sweeping gestures faded into silence. (c)<br />Q:<br />Of all the people in the world, only Arobynn knew the absolute truth. (c)<br />Q:<br />She couldn’t tell what was worse: a quick beheading, or yielding to the king. (c)<br />Q:<br />The Mute Master had told her that people dealt with their pain in different ways—that some chose to drown it, some chose to love it, and some chose to let it turn into rage. (с)<br />Q:<br />The history that lay between them, dark and twisted and full of secrets, was forged by more than just gold. (c)<br /><br /><b>And into her being so very fond of gifts with which he's trying to ingratiate himself into good terms with her. Does she love her trinkets!</b><br />Q:<br />But she couldn’t contain her squeal when she opened the box and found two gold hair combs glinting at her. They were exquisite, formed like sharp fish fins, each point accentuated with a sliver of sapphire. (c) Oh, gosh)<br />Q:<br />... she beamed at her reflection. Exotic, beguiling, imperious. (с)<br />Q:<br />An emerald-and-gold brooch glittered in the gray afternoon light. It was stunning, the work of a master craftsman—and she instantly knew what dresses and tunics it would best complement. (c)<br /><br /><b>Manicure troubles insight:</b><br />Q:<br />when her attention shifted to her hands—to her shredded cuticles and jagged nails. She let out a low hiss, (c)<br />Q:<br />She glanced again at her hair and nails. A very unkempt, wild-looking pet.<br />She strode into her dressing room. She’d decide what to do about Doneval and his agenda later. For now, not even the rain would keep her from a little pampering. (c)<br />Q:<br />... they didn’t trade in gold. No, they coveted things like dreams and memories and souls. (c)<br />And many other breathtaking things:<br />Q:<br />“You look beautiful. Though I bet you already know that.” She most certainly did. (c)<br />Q:<br />She was Adarlan’s Assassin; she’d freed slaves and stolen Asterion horses and won the respect of the Mute Master. Surely she could do something better than go to bed early. (c)<br />Q:<br />Some things are more important than death. (c)<br />Q:<br />“My name is Wind... And Rain. And Bone and Dust. My name is a snippet of a half-remembered song.”...<br />“I have no name, ... I am whoever the keepers of my fate tell me to be.” (c)<br />Q:<br />I don’t know how to be your friend yet. I don’t know if I know how to be anyone’s friend. (c)<br />Q:<br />The rooftop of her new apartment looked out over the Avery River, and Celaena sat on the walled edge, her legs dangling off the side. The stone beneath her was chill and damp, but the rain had stopped during the night, and fierce winds had blown the clouds away as the stars faded and the sky lightened.<br />The sun broke over the horizon, flooding the snaking arm of the Avery with light. It became a living band of gold. ...<br />She inhaled the damp morning air, letting it wash through her. Seated on the roof ledge, she felt wonderfully insignificant—a mere speck in the vastness of the great city. And yet all of it was hers for the taking. <br />Yes, the party had been delightful, but there was more to the world than that. Bigger things, more beautiful things, more real things. Her future was hers, and she had three trunks of gold hidden in her room that would solidify it. She could make of her life what she wanted.<br />Celaena leaned back on her hands, drinking in the awakening city. And as she watched the capital, she had the joyous feeling that the capital watched her back. (c)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7006166220112491632"><b>
  <blockquote>"How can I convince you to stay?"<br/>"You can't."</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486045054i/21874982._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This novella was so emotional I couldn't even think straight. I loved the vibes of this city and the sewerage systems were breathtaking that I turned the pages quickly to see how it ends. The Assassin and the Underworld would be the 4-star read for me if it was not for that predictable twist and ending. Sam, in this novella, is lovable. I saw a new side of him and liked it. The way he declared his love for Celaena is cute and undeniably touching.<br/><br/>A</span>
  <span id="freeText7006166220112491632" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>"How can I convince you to stay?"<br>"You can't."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486045054i/21874982._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This novella was so emotional I couldn't even think straight. I loved the vibes of this city and the sewerage systems were breathtaking that I turned the pages quickly to see how it ends. The Assassin and the Underworld would be the 4-star read for me if it was not for that predictable twist and ending. Sam, in this novella, is lovable. I saw a new side of him and liked it. The way he declared his love for Celaena is cute and undeniably touching.<br><br>Anyway, I was so scared when I finished this short story because I'd already known about what was going to happen and I was not ready. Mercy me.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I love you," he repeated, shaking her again. "I have for years. And he hurt you and made me watch because he's always know how I felt, too. But if I asked you to pick, you'd choose Arobynn, and I. Can't. Take. It.”</blockquote>

<span id="freeTextContainer5653111338371785580">I just can’t stop admiring Sarah J. Maas. The series of novella in <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b> keeps getting better and better. More action, more intrigue– <b>The Assassin and the Underworld</b> made me speechless! Sarah J. Maas made such a raw and powerful job in this novella.<br/><br/>I felt so many emotions while reading this. I felt sad, thrilled, excited, anxious, angry, swooning– everything. I’ve never felt these mixed emotions in a long while but in this novella, I experienced such a ride. I didn’t expect to hat</span>
  <span id="freeText5653111338371785580" style="display:none">I just can’t stop admiring Sarah J. Maas. The series of novella in <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b> keeps getting better and better. More action, more intrigue– <b>The Assassin and the Underworld</b> made me speechless! Sarah J. Maas made such a raw and powerful job in this novella.<br /><br />I felt so many emotions while reading this. I felt sad, thrilled, excited, anxious, angry, swooning– everything. I’ve never felt these mixed emotions in a long while but in this novella, I experienced such a ride. I didn’t expect to hate some of the characters here. I admit I already expected a betrayal and a deceit coming but still, what happened to Celaena broke me into pieces.<br /><br />The pacing of this novella is also plus. It’s fast paced and the important details were perfectly framed together. Also, <b>flawless plot!</b> I also love the <b>romance</b> between Sam and Celaena. It was sweet and not forced. <b>I ship them so bad!</b> Oh Sam…<br /><br />What more can be said about this novella? Everything is a form of masterpiece that only Sarah J. Maas can deliver!<br /><br />Rating: 5 Stars</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15840222072846535697">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br/><br/>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin'</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15840222072846535697" style="display:none">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br><br>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin's Blade</b>. And because I love <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3433047.Sarah_J_Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah J. Maas's</a>
</b> story telling and her writing, I am going to go ahead and read these beauties.<br><br>So, with that said, I am going to read and rate these so I can finally be completely caught up on The Throne of Glass Series: Throne of Glass, Crown of Midnight, Heir of Fire, Queen of Shadows, Empire of Storms, and Tower of Dawn.<br><br><u>The Assassin and the Underworld (Throne of Glass, #0.4)</u><br>I am set up for such heart break right now. I am completely and utterly in love with Sam. SPOILER ABOUT ME: I never really have shipped anyone with Celaena Sardothien. Dorian was cool and adorable, Chaol was a great rock for Celaena's personality, Rowan was LIFE to begin with, but then he kind of became "ehhh" to me. I mean, I am so happy that Celaena/Aelin is happy and with someone who cares about her and such, but I never really had an opinion if that makes sense.<br><br>Well, I have an opinion now. His name is <b>SAM</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512946053ra/24649426.gif" alt="" width="250" height="166" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, not that Sam but you know who I am talking about. <br><br>He cares SO MUCH for her, even when she is a little brat (which is most of the time). <br><br><i>"The moment I woke up after he beat me, I realized I <u>had</u> to leave. Because I was going to kill him if I didn't. But I couldn't." He studied her face. "Not until you came back. Not until I knew you were all right - until I saw that you were safe."</i><br><br><b>Just slit my heart open, Sam.</b><br><br>There is a lot of trickery in this book, but there is a lot of satisfaction as well. You'll want to kill Arobynn even more than you wanted to before you read this, but that is to be expected. <br><br>Oh and you'll also be setting yourself up for the worst thing in the world to happen, according to everyone I have talked to who has read the 5th installment of The Assassin's Blade. This should be horrible. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2817479879797595605">I can’t help but love the way that Arrobyn Hamel is written. Don’t get me wrong, I hate him just as much as everyone else who has read these novellas, But I absolutely love a good villain. He is so evil that he makes Celaena and Sam better characters. I love the romance we get to see blossoming between Celaena and Sam also. Sarah J. Maas wrote their characters beautifully and their romance matches.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2660603499" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2660603499" />
    <a title="Surbhi Das" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65787875-surbhi-das"><img alt="Surbhi Das" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588076555p2/65787875.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2660603499?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Surbhi Das" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Surbhi Das" href="/user/show/65787875-surbhi-das">Surbhi Das</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65787875-surbhi-das?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65787875-surbhi-das?shelf=novellas-and-short-stories">novellas-and-short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2660603499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11531890873295786528"><b>
  <i>“From today onward, I want to never be separated from you. Wherever you go, I go. Even if that means going to hell itself, wherever you are, that's where I want to be. Forever.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I don’t think I can write a coherent review of this book. My heart is already breaking into a million pieces and I am not ready for what is going to happen in the next novella. <br/><br/>Celaena is back to Rifthold after training with the silent assassins of the Red Desert and is all set to pay her debts to Arobynn Hamel and le</span>
  <span id="freeText11531890873295786528" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“From today onward, I want to never be separated from you. Wherever you go, I go. Even if that means going to hell itself, wherever you are, that's where I want to be. Forever.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I don’t think I can write a coherent review of this book. My heart is already breaking into a million pieces and I am not ready for what is going to happen in the next novella. <br /><br />Celaena is back to Rifthold after training with the silent assassins of the Red Desert and is all set to pay her debts to Arobynn Hamel and leave his house forever. In the months that she was away both Celaena and Sam have come to realise what they mean to each other but obviously they aren’t going to accept their feelings outright because god forbid Sarah J. Maas knows how to write angst and she just loves to make us reader squirm in torment. Anyways, the two of them begin to work on a mission together which involve killing a noble man from Melisande and I for one, loved the two of them in action together. They are absolutely amazing together and Sam oh! Sam, this man guys! He is the absolute best.<br /><br />Also, Lysandara shows up ahhh!!!! And she and Celaena. I can’t believe it’s the same Lysandara but it's so much fun to see the two of them interact. Their relationship grew in one of the most wonderfully written friendship later in the series but to see the bitter beginning of their relationship and how much the two women endured and grew in the years following their spat was very interesting and emotional. <br /><br />And Dorian and Chaol showed up…. I can’t stop squealing!! I know their names are not specifically mentioned but I know it was them in the harvest festival…. Because Dorian… because arrogance… because sapphire eyes and Chaol and his sword and his protectiveness towards Dorian… ahhhhh!<br /><br />Honestly, I am dreading to read the next novella “The Assassin and the Empire”. I know I said it before but I AM NOT READY! NOPE NOT EVEN IN THE LEAST!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“What's your name?" he asked above the roar of the music.<br /><br />She leaned close. "My name is Wind," she whispered. "And Rain. And Bone and Dust. My name is a snippet of a half-remembered song."<br /><br />He chuckled a low, delightful sound. She was drunk and silly, and so full of the glory of being young and alive and in the capital of the world that she could hardly contain herself.<br /><br />"I have no name," she purred. "I am whoever the keepers of my fate tell me to be."<br /><br />He grasped her by her wrist, running a thumb along the sensitive skin underneath. "Then let me call you Mine for a dance or two.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><a href="https://bemusedb.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Bemusedb/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/bibliophileSur/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/bemused._.bibliophile/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11531890873295786528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_849346148" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/849346148" />
    <a title="Tiffany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7571542-tiffany"><img alt="Tiffany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542787877p2/7571542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/849346148?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany" href="/user/show/7571542-tiffany">Tiffany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15713902-the-assassin-and-the-underworld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7571542-tiffany?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7571542-tiffany?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7571542-tiffany?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer849346148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2847112486049843920">Knowing what happens to Celaena, and what happens to Sam, it is getting increasingly harder for me to read on. I'm just getting more and more sad over what Arobynn does, and more and more sad that I like Sam so much. <br/><br/>This novella was very dramatic. The way that Arobynn attempts to make it up to Celaena, hearing about what had happened with Sam's punishment, and the betrayals and close calls with death...<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b><i>Sam swore violently and began yanking on the grate cover again. "Come on," he whispered, m</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2847112486049843920" style="display:none">Knowing what happens to Celaena, and what happens to Sam, it is getting increasingly harder for me to read on. I'm just getting more and more sad over what Arobynn does, and more and more sad that I like Sam so much. <br><br>This novella was very dramatic. The way that Arobynn attempts to make it up to Celaena, hearing about what had happened with Sam's punishment, and the betrayals and close calls with death...<br><br><blockquote>
  <b><i>Sam swore violently and began yanking on the grate cover again. "Come on," he whispered, more to himself than to her. "</i>Come on<i>."<br><br>The water was around her waist now, and over her chest a moment after that. Rain continued streaming in through the grate, blinding her senses. "Sam," she said.<br><br>"I'm trying!"<br><br>Sam," she repeated.<br><br>"No," he spat, hearing her tone. "</i>No.<i>"</i></b>
</blockquote><br><br>Celanea returns from the desert and is immediately hired and asks Sam to help her. She and Sam think that they are both working for a cause they approve of, but they really don't know much about it until it's too late. Celaena has also returned with enough gold to pay for her freedom, but she struggles with this decision when Arobynn begins showering her with gifts in an attempt to seek her forgiveness. <br><br>I don't even understand what happened that made Arobynn turn on Celaena in the first place. Why? And what really happened with Ben because I feel that's where it had to have began. Why was she sent on the errand to the Pirate Lord not having any clue as to why she was really there when up until that point, she was Arobynn's protegee and number one? Why did he <i>seem</i> to regret what he had done to her when she came back? What is/was Celaena to Arobynn, and what was it that made him turn against her?! I don't feel that it can be about Sam because Arobynn sent them to the islands together without them knowing his plans for why they were truly there while Celaena and Sam were still enemies.<br><br>I have a feeling, just from the titles of the remaining novellas, that the next one is when the fate that we already know these two have will take place. I'm sort of depressed about it. I've grown to like them to the point where I'm hoping that what I know will happen will turn out to be just what we <i>think</i> happened. <br><br>There's a moment of crossover in this story when Celaena is at a party and <i>we</i> know that the masked strangers she meets are in fact Dorian and Chaol...awww, how cute that they all met so long before their story takes place. Sort of. I'm team Sam now and I'm kind of pissed about that. <br><br>I also feel that Celaena was a bit of a brat in the past. She was unnecessarily mean, A LOT. I don't know what Sam originally saw in her considering she would have gladly killed him in his sleep...I didn't feel she deserved his loyalty really. <br><br>In the end, I loved this one...as I've loved them all. I guess I <i>have</i> to read on as much as I'd like to pretend that the story ends here. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429831ra/861395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2847112486049843920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_984726572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984726572" />
    <a title="Marga " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6418118-marga"><img alt="Marga " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423326869p2/6418118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/984726572?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marga " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marga " href="/user/show/6418118-marga">Marga </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=2014-buddy-reads">2014-buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=2014-favorites">2014-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=novellas-short-stories">novellas-short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=mmc-read-books">mmc-read-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6418118-marga?shelf=too-much-feels">too-much-feels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer984726572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4960520857029015577"><blockquote>
  <i>"In the silence of her bedroom, she swore an oath to the moonlight that if Sam were hurt, no force in the world would her back from slaughtering everyone responsible." </i>
</blockquote> <br/>I think this is the best novella so far. I still have to read the last one but this.. This made me love Sam a whole lot. I can't convey enough how much my heart hurts now..<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"The moment I woke up after he beat me, I realized I have to leave. Because I was going to kill him if I didn't. But I couldn't." He studied her face. "</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4960520857029015577" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"In the silence of her bedroom, she swore an oath to the moonlight that if Sam were hurt, no force in the world would her back from slaughtering everyone responsible." </i>
</blockquote> <br />I think this is the best novella so far. I still have to read the last one but this.. This made me love Sam a whole lot. I can't convey enough how much my heart hurts now..<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"The moment I woke up after he beat me, I realized I have to leave. Because I was going to kill him if I didn't. But I couldn't." He studied her face. "Not until you came back. Not until I know you were alright- until I saw that you were safe." </i>
</blockquote> <br />My heart. Be ready. You're going to get broken. I just knew it. T_T And I really hate Arobynn!!!!Argh.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I love you," he repeated shaking her again. "I have for years. And he hurt you and made me watch because he's always known how I felt, too. And if I asked you to pick, you'd choose Arobynn, and I. Can't. Take. It."</i>
</blockquote><br />Really, I think my masochistic side is showing because even if it'll hurt so much, I want to read the last novella. Ahhhh. Bring it on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4960520857029015577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2208261060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3492481321431280333"><blockquote>
  <b>“In the silence of her bedroom, she swore an oath to the moonlight that if Sam were hurt, no force in the world would hold her back from slaughtering everyone responsible.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I don’t think I have ever loved Sam more than I loved him in this book. Such a sweetheart! The sewer scene had me screaming, even though I knew she survives (Obviously) but still it kept me on my toes. And I just keep hating Arobynn more and more each day. No matter what this guy does, I’ll always have a burning hatred for</span>
  <span id="freeText3492481321431280333" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“In the silence of her bedroom, she swore an oath to the moonlight that if Sam were hurt, no force in the world would hold her back from slaughtering everyone responsible.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I don’t think I have ever loved Sam more than I loved him in this book. Such a sweetheart! The sewer scene had me screaming, even though I knew she survives (Obviously) but still it kept me on my toes. And I just keep hating Arobynn more and more each day. No matter what this guy does, I’ll always have a burning hatred for him.<br><br>And can we talk about Dorian and Chaol’s mini appearance?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513762243ra/24719034.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Either way, this one was one of my favorites. My heart hurts everytime I think about the last novella. The fact that I have to review that one is killing me.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BTS9R1p2435Cffjg+kugc9b3JdnUgk5FI3T749jLKmLTRfhnkFWhY+65BeXzPVkzm+BzBrwmYPHWHKHRtEGiaA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/19111271-the-assassin-and-the-underworld">Quotes from The Assassin and ...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;What's your name?" he asked above the roar of the music.<br /><br />She leaned close. "My name is Wind," she whispered. "And Rain. And Bone and Dust. My name is a snippet of a half-remembered song."<br /><br />He chuckled a low, delightful sound. She was drunk and silly, and so full of the glory of being young and alive and in the capital of the world that she could hardly contain herself.<br /><br />"I have no name," she purred. "I am whoever the keepers of my fate tell me to be."<br /><br />He grasped her by her wrist, running a thumb along the sensitive sknin underneath. "Then let me call you Mine for a dance or two.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/927806-what-s-your-name-he-asked-above-the-roar-of-the">310 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Please don't go."<br />He let out an uneven breath. "You'll be fine without me. You always have been."<br />Maybe once, but not now. "How can I convince you to stay?"<br />"You can't."<br />She threw down the torch. "Do you want me to beg, is that it?"<br />"No-never."<br />"Then tell me-"<br />"What more can I say?" he exploded, his whisper rough and harsh "I’ve already told you everything—I’ve already told you that if I stay here, if I have to live with Arobynn, I'll snap his damned neck.”<br />“But why? Why can’t you let it go?”<br />He grabbed her shoulders and shook her. “Because I love you!”<br />Her mouth fell open.<br />“I love you,” he repeated, shaking her again. “I have for years. And he hurt you and made me watch because he’s always known how I felt, too. But if I asked you to pick, you’d choose Arobynn, and I. Can’t. Take. It.”<br />The only sounds were their breathing, an uneven beat against the rushing of the sewer river.<br />“You’re a damned idiot,” she breathed, grabbing the front of his tunic. “You’re a moron and an ass and a damned idiot.” He looked like she had hit him. But she went on, and grasped both sides of his face, "Because I'd pick you."<br />And then she kissed him.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/700309-please-don-t-go-he-let-out-an-uneven-breath-you-ll">272 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/19111271-the-assassin-and-the-underworld">More quotes&hellip;</a>
